  <a href="#other_reviews" class="actionLinkLite votes">
      <span itemprop="ratingCount" title="279205" class="value-title">279,205 Ratings</span>
</a>  <span class="greyText"> · </span>

<div id="descriptionContainer">
      <div style="right:0" class="readable stacked" id="description">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer16241891207226406770">Coraline lives with her preoccupied parents in part of a huge old house--a house so huge that other people live in it, too... round, old former actresses Miss Spink and Miss Forcible and their aging Highland terriers ("We trod the boards, luvvy") and the mustachioed old man under the roof ("'The reason you cannot see the mouse circus,' said the man upstairs, 'is that the m</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16241891207226406770">Coraline lives with her preoccupied parents in part of a huge old house--a house so huge that other people live in it, too... round, old former actresses Miss Spink and Miss Forcible and their aging Highland terriers ("We trod the boards, luvvy") and the mustachioed old man under the roof ("'The reason you cannot see the mouse circus,' said the man upstairs, 'is that the mice are not yet ready and rehearsed.'") Coraline contents herself for weeks with exploring the vast garden and grounds. But with a little rain she becomes bored--so bored that she begins to count everything blue (153), the windows (21), and the doors (14). And it is the 14th door that--sometimes blocked with a wall of bricks--opens up for Coraline into an entirely alternate universe. Now, if you're thinking fondly of <em>The Lion, the Witch, and the Wardrobe</em> or <em>Alice's Adventures in Wonderland</em>, you're on the wrong track. Neil Gaiman's <em>Coraline</em> is far darker, far stranger, playing on our deepest fears. And, like Roald Dahl's work, it is delicious. <p> What's on the other side of the door? A distorted-mirror world, containing presumably everything Coraline has ever dreamed of... people who pronounce her name correctly (not "Caroline"), delicious meals (not like her father's overblown "recipes"), an unusually pink and green bedroom (not like her dull one), and plenty of horrible (very un-boring) marvels, like a man made out of live rats. The creepiest part, however, is her mirrored parents, her "other mother" and her "other father"--people who look just like her own parents, but with big, shiny, black button eyes, paper-white skin... and a keen desire to keep her on <em>their</em> side of the door. To make creepy creepier, <em>Coraline</em> has been illustrated masterfully in scritchy, terrifying ink drawings by British mixed-media artist and Sandman cover illustrator Dave McKean. This delightful, funny, haunting, scary as heck, fairy-tale novel is about as fine as they come. Highly recommended. (Ages 11 and older) <em>--Karin Snelson</em></p></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16241891207226406770">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown">
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_61530172">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/61530172" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/922495-patrick" class="left imgcol" title="Patrick"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" alt="Patrick" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/61530172?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 06, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/922495-patrick" class="user" title="Patrick">Patrick</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer61530172">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6531111764532115678">I've read this book many different times in many different ways. <br /><br />I read it off the page when it first came out. Later, I listened to Gaiman's narration of the audiobook when I was sequestered in the north woods of Wisconsin in a desperate attempt to finish book two. I watched the movie and enjoyed it. <br /><br />My most recent experience of the book was listening to it with my little boy on a long car ride. I wasn't sure he'd be able to get into it. Not because of the vocabulary. He's very sharp for being</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6531111764532115678">I've read this book many different times in many different ways. <br /><br />I read it off the page when it first came out. Later, I listened to Gaiman's narration of the audiobook when I was sequestered in the north woods of Wisconsin in a desperate attempt to finish book two. I watched the movie and enjoyed it. <br /><br />My most recent experience of the book was listening to it with my little boy on a long car ride. I wasn't sure he'd be able to get into it. Not because of the vocabulary. He's very sharp for being 4.5. He's good with words. But sometimes he gets a little scared. <br /><br />Despite my worries, he seemed to enjoy it. He paid attention, attention, asking for us to turn it back on after we stopped by the side of the road. A day later, he excitedly told me all about the story, apparently forgetting I'd been in the car too. <br /><br />All of that was months ago. Fast forward to now.... <br /><br />* * *<br /><br />"Dad," Oot said. "Do you know the guy who wrote Coraline?"<br /><br />The question caught me by surprise. The two of us were driving to a party together, a friend was having a bonfire and I was amazed that he was thinking about anything other than smores.<br /><br />"I do," I said. "His name is Neil Gaiman." <br /><br />"Do you have his phone number?" he asked.<br /><br />"No," I said.<br /><br />"Do you know where he lives?"<br /><br />"I do," I said.<br /><br />"Are you his friend?"<br /><br />That brought me up short. For Oot, that's a simple question. If you meet someone and play with them, they're you're friend. Easy. <br /><br />For adults these things are harder. And it's doubly hard for me these days. My life has changed so much over the last five years, and my previously established metric for friendship doesn't work very well any more. <br /><br />You see, for the majority of my life, a friend was someone who would, say, help me move a couch. Someone you could bum 10 dollars off of if you needed to. A friend was someone who felt comfortable enough to come over to my house without calling first. Then, if I wasn't home, they would let themselves in, eat out of my fridge, and start watching TV. <br /><br />While I'm terribly fond of him, Neil Gaiman has never done any of these things. <br /><br />Then again, neither have any of the other authors I've met over the last few years. I'm painfully aware of the need for new friendship metrics, but I haven't managed to develop a good set yet.<br /><br />That won't make any sense to my boy, but still, I try to be honest with him whenever I can. "I don't know if we're friends," I say. "But we're colleagues."<br /><br />"What's a colleagues?" he asks, right on cue. <br /><br />"That means we know each other and do the same job," I explain. <br /><br />"Oh yes," he says. "You're both authors." <br /><br />It makes me proud when he says that. I'm proud that my boy knows I write books. <br /><br />"Do you know his address?" Oot asks, and it takes me a while to realize that he's returning to his previous line of questioning. <br /><br />"I do," I said, not bothering to point out that knowing where someone lives and knowing their address is pretty much the same thing.<br /><br />"Can you send him a letter?" <br /><br />"I could," I say. <br /><br />Oot pauses for a moment then, and I realize that this has been the point of the whole conversation. He wants to send Neil Gaiman a message. <br /><br />"What would you like me to write to him?" I ask. <br /><br />"You should tell him he *sure* knows how to write a scary story...."<br /><br />* * *<br /><br />So there you go. You don't really need me to tell you how I feel about one of Gaiman's books at this point. You know I love his writing. <br /><br />Instead, I'm offering up my boy's unvarnished opinion. Did he think the story was scary? Absolutely. But he still wanted us to turn it back on as soon as we were back in the car. <br /><br />What's more, he was still thinking about Coraline months later. And it was the first book where he's ever shown any interest in contacting the author. <br /><br />So. Bravo, Neil Gaiman. You've managed to win over two generations of the Rothfuss household.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6531111764532115678">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_101867805">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/101867805" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya" class="left imgcol" title="Nataliya"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1395089173p2/3672777.jpg" alt="Nataliya" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/101867805?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 04, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya" class="user" title="Nataliya">Nataliya</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Gaiman and excellent YA dark fantasy</span></div>

        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=awesome-kickass-heroines" class="actionLinkLite">awesome-kickass-heroines</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=hugo-nebula" class="actionLinkLite">hugo-nebula</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=i-also-saw-the-film" class="actionLinkLite">i-also-saw-the-film</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=for-my-future-hypothetical-daughter" class="actionLinkLite">for-my-future-hypothetical-daughter</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=locus-winner" class="actionLinkLite">locus-winner</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer101867805">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18029607501149103546"><em>Coraline</em> is a <strong>short but delightfully dark and creepy book</strong> that just happens to feature one of my absolute favorite characters. <strong> <em>Is it wrong that I want to be Coraline's best friend???<br /></em> </strong><br /><img width="220" height="120" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334722i/694001._SX540_.png" /><img width="170" height="120" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334722i/694002.jpg" /><blockquote> <em> “Because,' she said, 'when you're scared but you still do it anyway, that's brave.” </em> </blockquote> Coraline is clever, quirky, curious and adventurous, brave and determined, independent, stubborn to no end, a bit reckless and not scared of danger. She will <strong>NEVER</strong> leave any mysterious doors locked and uninvestigated. <strong> <em> <u>In short</u></em></strong></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText18029607501149103546"><em>Coraline</em> is a <strong>short but delightfully dark and creepy book</strong> that just happens to feature one of my absolute favorite characters. <strong>
  <em>Is it wrong that I want to be Coraline's best friend???<br /></em>
</strong><br /><img width="220" height="120" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334722i/694001._SX540_.png" /><img width="170" height="120" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334722i/694002.jpg" /><blockquote> <em> “Because,' she said, 'when you're scared but you still do it anyway, that's brave.” </em>
</blockquote> Coraline is clever, quirky, curious and adventurous, brave and determined, independent, stubborn to no end, a bit reckless and not scared of danger. She will <strong>NEVER</strong> leave any mysterious doors locked and uninvestigated. <strong>
  <em>
    <u>In short, she is what I hope my future (hypothetical) daughter is going to be like.</u>
  </em>
</strong> Out of boredom due to rainy days and parental inattention, Coraline sets out on a scary but awesome adventure. She bites off (almost) more than she can chew, but comes out of it a winner and just a bit more grown-up and mature (but luckily not in a dreadful moralistic way). <blockquote>
  <em>"Nothing’s changed. You’ll go home. You’ll be bored. You’ll be ignored. No one will listen to you, really listen to you. You’re too clever and too quiet for them to understand. They don’t even get your name right."</em>
</blockquote> The story is intense and sinister, and yet really fun. <strong>With his dark fairy-tales <em>Coraline</em> and <em>The Graveyard Book</em>, Gaiman proves that he has mastered the art of writing perfect non-condescending children's books that also appeal to adults.</strong> He is not afraid of making a kids' book scary; he knows kids can handle it quite well. The "Other" world he creates is eerie and surreal, with a dreamlike quality - <em>the kind of dream from which you wake up screaming. </em>But the story is also full of humor and has the Cat!<br /><br />....... <img width="250" height="200" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380334723i/694003.jpg" />............<br /><br />I guess I have a weakness for <strong>amazing book-cats</strong> (it must be the <em>Alice in Wonderland</em> influence on my young pliable mind back in 1980s). I adore the wisdom, independence, and a bit of condescending attitude they give humans. <blockquote> <em>"We... we could be friends, you know," said Coraline.<br />"We COULD be rare specimens of an exotic breed of African dancing elephants," said the cat. "But we're not. At least," it added cattily, after darting a brief look at Coraline, "I'M not."</em>
</blockquote> -----------<br />The language of the book is simple and sparing, and fits the story perfectly. <em>Coraline</em> is one of the books that are just meant to be read aloud. Overall, a great story that fully deserves the <strong>5-star</strong> rating.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="18029607501149103546">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_197529418">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/197529418" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6014887-richard" class="left imgcol" title="Richard"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1389632385p2/6014887.jpg" alt="Richard" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/197529418?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 26, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6014887-richard" class="user" title="Richard">Richard</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=children-s-lit" class="actionLinkLite">children-s-lit</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6014887-richard?shelf=2011" class="actionLinkLite">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer197529418">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17268398596035167766">I saw the film before I read the book, which is not how I like to do things, as it can often be like taping a hockey game and having someone tell you the final score before you've had a chance to see the game for yourself. However, I can say that seeing the film first didn't really spoil the book for me. <br /><br />Coraline starts off rather slowly but this independent, thoughtful, odd, distant, misunderstood child soon gains the reader's sympathy. This becomes more intense as Coraline gets more deeply enm</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17268398596035167766">I saw the film before I read the book, which is not how I like to do things, as it can often be like taping a hockey game and having someone tell you the final score before you've had a chance to see the game for yourself. However, I can say that seeing the film first didn't really spoil the book for me. <br /><br />Coraline starts off rather slowly but this independent, thoughtful, odd, distant, misunderstood child soon gains the reader's sympathy. This becomes more intense as Coraline gets more deeply enmeshed in danger. <br /><br />Gaiman does a good job of characterization. We see the characters through the eyes of a little girl who is remarkably intelligent and yet doesn't understand everything the adults do or say. Many of the adults are eccentric in a Dickensian sort of way; they deal with others when they have to but are firmly ensconced in their own little worlds. And so they see Coraline as an oddity too. <br /><br />The cat is perhaps my favourite character of all. Gaiman knows cats well; they appear elsewhere in his works. And this one is the genuine article: superior, stand-offish, wilful, easily offended, and yet a true friend.<br /><br />Gaiman makes this a children's book that will appeal to adults as well. It doesn't talk down to children. Not everything is spelled out or explained away. We don't really know, for example, who the Other Mother is or where she came from. As the book progresses we get hints, but not a "back-story." And that's just fine--although I have to admit, I'm curious. Any chance of a sequel or a prequel, Neil?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17268398596035167766">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_280140805">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280140805" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5691412-meg" class="left imgcol" title="Meg ?"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1356897271p2/5691412.jpg" alt="Meg ?" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/280140805?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 12, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5691412-meg" class="user" title="Meg ?">Meg ?</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5691412-meg?shelf=e-books" class="actionLinkLite">e-books</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5691412-meg?shelf=z-2012-reads" class="actionLinkLite">z-2012-reads</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5691412-meg?shelf=books-2-movies" class="actionLinkLite">books-2-movies</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer280140805">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10187200040177319187"><br />I've been looking for that book that would satisfy my craving to be creeped out, and sadly a few books I tried recently didn't do it for me. I didn't expect anything with this book, and that little shiver down my spine that has been evading me? This book gave it to me!<br /><br /><br />I was not a huge fan of <em>American Gods</em>, but I promised that I would give Neil Gaiman another shot someday. I figured if I enjoyed anything of his it would be this book. Despite my gripes with <em>American Gods</em> I couldn't deny that I fou</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10187200040177319187"><br />I've been looking for that book that would satisfy my craving to be creeped out, and sadly a few books I tried recently didn't do it for me. I didn't expect anything with this book, and that little shiver down my spine that has been evading me? This book gave it to me!<br /><br /><br />I was not a huge fan of <em>American Gods</em>, but I promised that I would give Neil Gaiman another shot someday. I figured if I enjoyed anything of his it would be this book. Despite my gripes with <em>American Gods</em> I couldn't deny that I found Gaiman to be a great storyteller. This book definitely confirms that I was right about that.<br /><br /><br />Coraline is a young girl who loves to explore and finds a locked door in her house. Her mother shows her that there is nothing there by unlocking the door and revealing a brick wall behind the door. However, a while later she tries to open the door again and enters a mysterious passageway that leads her to another house that looks like her own house. She meets a woman who refers to herself as Coraline's "other mother". When she returns home from this alternate world she realizes that her parents are gone and she must rescue them. Coraline is tempted into this new world where everything seems better. At her real home she is fighting the computer for her father's attention. She has to choose where to stay, and which life she really wants.<br /><br /><br />This book is only 99 pages on the Nook so I don't really want to give too much away. It's a very quick, but chilling read in my opinion. I loved the dialog between Coraline and all of the other characters, particularly the cat. The creepy graphics added to the eeriness of this book. I feel like this could be a fun book to read with my son around Halloween.<br /><br /><br />I also love how smart Coraline was in the end. She really learned the age old lesson about the grass always being greener. Love this quote: <br /><br /><em>“I don't want whatever I want. Nobody does. Not really. What kind of fun would it be if I just got everything I ever wanted just like that, and it didn't mean anything? What then?” </em><br />Such a wise thing to think coming from a young girl. I don't think Coraline's actual age is ever revealed in this book, but either way she's young enough to make that an impressive statement.<br /><br /><br />I really liked this book, and would recommend it. It's short, cute, fun, and creepy. Don't get me wrong. This book wasn't terrifying or anything like that, but for a children's book I was impressed with how much I actually felt scared for Coraline being all alone in this strange world.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="10187200040177319187">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_811683443">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/811683443" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/25353295-carmen" class="left imgcol" title="Carmen"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1412617445p2/25353295.jpg" alt="Carmen" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/811683443?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 26, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/25353295-carmen" class="user" title="Carmen">Carmen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1061252.Coraline" title="Hardcover 9780747558538" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Kids; Parents</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Carmen by: </span>
      Theresa
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=children" class="actionLinkLite">children</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/25353295-carmen?shelf=traditionally-published" class="actionLinkLite">traditionally-published</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer811683443">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7091259722776411921"><em>Coraline was woken by the mid-morning sun, full on her face.<br /><br />For a moment she felt utterly dislocated. She did not know where she was; she was not entirely sure WHO she was. It is astonishing just how much of what we are can be tied to the beds we wake up in in the morning, and it is astonishing how fragile that can be.</em><br /><br />This is like Stephen King's <a title="It by Stephen King" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/830502.It">It</a> re-written for children.<br /><br />I adore Stephen King, obviously, and I highly enjoyed this creepy and horrifying children's book that Gaiman has written.<br /><br />Cora</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7091259722776411921"><em>Coraline was woken by the mid-morning sun, full on her face.<br /><br />For a moment she felt utterly dislocated. She did not know where she was; she was not entirely sure WHO she was. It is astonishing just how much of what we are can be tied to the beds we wake up in in the morning, and it is astonishing how fragile that can be.</em><br /><br />This is like Stephen King's <a title="It by Stephen King" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/830502.It">It</a> re-written for children.<br /><br />I adore Stephen King, obviously, and I highly enjoyed this creepy and horrifying children's book that Gaiman has written.<br /><br />Coraline is a little girl who is rather introverted. This means she is ignored by adults a lot. Most of them don't even know her real name - Coraline - and instead, keep erroneously calling her Caroline. Her parents work a lot and don't spend a lot of time with Coraline.<br /><br />One day, Coraline discovers a secret door that leads into a world just like her own. There's her bedroom, slightly off-color. There's her bed. And there's her 'other mother' with black button eyes and fingers that are constantly twitching and writhing.<br /><br />Her other mother loves her. Wants her to stay. Stay forever. There's only one thing Coraline has to do, and her other mother promises it won't hurt at all...<br />...<br /><br />Seriously creepy and disturbing book. You might want to vet this for your children if you worry about that sort of thing. When I say "Stephen King for children," I am not joking. This book is dark and full of very disturbing and unsettling images.<br /><br />I think any adult or child could really love this book. It is a great book.<br /><br />I think some of my favorite books are books where:<br /><br /><em>They were astonishingly heavy - almost too heavy for a girl to lift, even using all her strength, but she managed. She didn't have any choice.</em><br /><br />a female character does something challenging or disgusting or scary because she has to. There's no other option - she must be strong and brave or die. No fucking around. This is so reminiscent of my life that I love seeing it in my fiction. Especially when (like here) everything turns out okay in the end and the story has a happy ending. Female characters with agency and gumption float my boat. Coraline has that in spades. She's a great little heroine.<br /><br />There are some things that are going to bother an adult reader. For example, a certain twist <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[the location of Coraline's REAL parents <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> will be obviously to an adult reader LONG before Coraline ever figures it out.<br /><br />Also, you will probably be shaking your head frequently and wondering why adults are so goshdarn useless in children's literature.<br /><br />Another drawback of the book for me is the utter villainization and denigration of rats. Rats are lovely creatures. Why are they always demonized in fiction? This is a travesty. You're not winning any points with me, Mr. Gaiman. And you're teaching children to hate and fear rats when really rats are a delightful pet for children to have. Friendly, sweet, smart, and cuddly. Like very tiny dogs and with much less upkeep and expense.<br /><br />Little things in the book I love. For instance, Coraline hates "real food" (what she calls 'recipes') and instead lives on stuff like microwaved frozen pizza and microwaved frozen French fries. She is delighted when, while visiting the neighbors, she is served limeade.<br /><br /><em>For tea she went down to see Misses Spink and Forcible. She had three digestive biscuits, a glass of limeade, and a cup of weak tea. The limeade was very interesting. It didn't taste anything like limes. It tasted bright green and vaguely chemical. Coraline liked it enormously. She wished they had it at home.</em><br /><br />LOL So funny and so true of children. I'm glad Gaiman isn't trying to make Coraline into a 'little adult.' And, now that I think about it, nor is he trying to force some kind of 'healthy eating' agenda down readers' throats. Ugh, I hate that shit. Instead, he's absolutely captured childhood with perfection.<br /><br />I enjoy Gaiman's writing, which is not very detailed, but is pleasing nonetheless.<br /><br /><em>The mist hung like blindness around the house.</em><br /><br />How about this passage, talking about rain:<br /><br /><em>Coraline went over to the window and watched the rain come down. It wasn't the kind of rain you could go out in, it was the other kind, the kind that threw itself down from the sky and splashed where it landed. It was rain that meant business, and currently its business was turning the garden into a muddy, wet, soup.</em><br />...<br /><br />Tl;dr - A delightful, very creepy and haunting story that will have both adults and children turning on the nightlights after darkness falls. A great, smart heroine who takes the initiative and acts with purpose. Highly recommended.<br /><br />P.S. I wonder if the 'other mother' in this book was called The Beldam after <em>La belle dame sans merci.</em> *shrug* Something to ponder.<br /><br />P.P.S. Thanks, Chrissie, for this cool link of people reading Coraline!<br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://mousecircus.com/coraline-videos.aspx?VideoID=24" target="_blank">http://mousecircus.com/coraline-video...</a><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7091259722776411921">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/551397982?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 02, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh" class="user" title="Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh">Florence (Lefty) MacIntosh</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone with the heart of a child – Gaiman fans</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Florence (Lefty) by: </span>
      Mary MacAskill
  </div>



          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/10856439-florence-lefty-macintosh?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer551397982">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6189212886670829108">Deliciously disturbing, a modern fairytale with a surrealistic feel. I mean you’re stuck in an alternate dimension with parents with sewed on buttons for eyes, friendless except for a talking cat with a bad attitude. Coraline is totally believable; a bored sweet kid who gets herself into and out of a terrifying situation by being gutsy &amp; resourceful. So unless you figure you’ve outgrown fairytales (which is kind of a shame) what’s not to like about it?<br /><br />Nasty flu &amp; a crummy day at work had</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6189212886670829108">Deliciously disturbing, a modern fairytale with a surrealistic feel. I mean you’re stuck in an alternate dimension with parents with sewed on buttons for eyes, friendless except for a talking cat with a bad attitude. Coraline is totally believable; a bored sweet kid who gets herself into and out of a terrifying situation by being gutsy &amp; resourceful. So unless you figure you’ve outgrown fairytales (which is kind of a shame) what’s not to like about it?<br /><br />Nasty flu &amp; a crummy day at work had me pretty well pissed off at the world. Crawled into bed early in a definite funk, figured I’d try a few pages of this little novella. Riveted I read it cover to cover. Snuggled under a pile of blankets, suitable ambience provided by a fierce rainstorm slashing at my windowpane I felt like I was ten again. Bliss. Finished in a couple of hours,when I drifted off to sleep I was feeling almost human. Sometimes a good story cures all that ails ya:)<br /><br />I’m a Gaiman fan so take this with a grain of salt. People tend to disdain contemporary novels so give it another 50 years. I’m betting this will earn its place among classics like Hansel &amp; Gretel, Alice In Wonderland &amp; Pinocchio. Okay, maybe I'm stretching it with Pinocchio…<br /><br /><strong>For the genre of creepy fairytales 4 ½ stars.</strong><br />________________________________________<br /><em>“She stepped out of the way as the thing clicked and scuttled past her and out of the house, running crablike on its too-many tapping, clicking, scurrying feet. She knew what it was, and she knew what it was after. Five-footed, crimson-nailed, the color of bone.”<em></em></em></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6189212886670829108">...more</a>

    	<a href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune" alt="BrokenTune"><img alt="10592271" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1391017756p1/10592271.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="xhr_comment_body">
    <a href="/user/show/10592271-brokentune" style="font-weight:bold">BrokenTune</a>

      
<span id="freeTextContainer17823288642515863340">BookLikes is ok. It's different, needs getting used to, but I really like that you can save work-in-progress when writing a review. <br /><br />All posts are base</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17823288642515863340">BookLikes is ok. It's different, needs getting used to, but I really like that you can save work-in-progress when writing a review. <br /><br />All posts are based on the blog which makes it easy to control your own stuff, but makes it a bit more difficult to track conversations on other people's blogs. (I'm not sure if it posts on other people's blogs tracks on your timeline.)<br /><br />There is no facility for groups or personal messaging at the moment, and there are some other features that GR has which would be nice to replicate on BL - like seeing your friends reviews listed first on a book page, consolidated book pages (at the moment each edition has a separate page), author pages etc.<br />But the good news is that the BL owners are putting a lot of work into improving the site and are considering the requests from users. There is a whole blog about BL improvements that is just a simple wishlist. And so far BL have delivered improvements on a weekly basis - always released on Thursdays - and communicated to everyone. Their communication is quite good actually. I email about a query and had a response within 24 hours.<br /><br />With respect to techi-ness, I can't handle/be bothered with complicated programming either. Even the limited html on GR was unknown to me at first. Thankfully, there is not that much programming on BL unless you really want to individualise your blog. And if you do, there are already some existing manuals/instructions on how to change layout etc. from people who have migrated there recently.<br /><br />In short I like it!<br /><br />I'm no longer posting reviews on GR, only on BL. It tried to just add a link in the review box for my recent reads, but am not convinced that they show in my update feed. I may also re-think other updates such as adding to shelves as this to could add to the stats that Amazon will make use of. (Not that I hate Amazon, but I'd like there to be a limit to Amazon monitoring my life...)<br /><br />The only reason I haven't migrated completely is that I do want to keep in touch with friends on GR who aren't on BL. <br /><br />Have you tried BL yet?</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17823288642515863340">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_13048312">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/13048312" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/766524-robert-beveridge" class="left imgcol" title="Robert Beveridge"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1286387835p2/766524.jpg" alt="Robert Beveridge" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/13048312?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 21, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/766524-robert-beveridge" class="user" title="Robert Beveridge">Robert Beveridge</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/766524-robert-beveridge?shelf=finished" class="actionLinkLite">finished</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/766524-robert-beveridge?shelf=cle-pub-lib" class="actionLinkLite">cle-pub-lib</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer13048312">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2857987455198246243">Neil Gaiman, Coraline (Harper, 2002)<br /><br />I'm not exactly sure what to say about this minor gem. It's a kids' book, but not really a kids' book. It's a fantasy/horror novel, but not a fantasy/horror novel. It has minor similarities to about a hundred books to be found over the ages, both children's and adult, but nothing strong enough to be called an influence (at least, not one that wears its heart on its sleeve). About the best thing I can come up with would be a much darker version of Roald Dahl's</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2857987455198246243">Neil Gaiman, Coraline (Harper, 2002)<br /><br />I'm not exactly sure what to say about this minor gem. It's a kids' book, but not really a kids' book. It's a fantasy/horror novel, but not a fantasy/horror novel. It has minor similarities to about a hundred books to be found over the ages, both children's and adult, but nothing strong enough to be called an influence (at least, not one that wears its heart on its sleeve). About the best thing I can come up with would be a much darker version of Roald Dahl's Matilda with a leavening of The Secret Garden, a touch or two of Neverwhere, and a dash of Wendy Walker's The Secret Service just for flair. And a large number of flavors running underneath you will sense but not really be able to put your finger on.<br /><br />Coraline is a girl who's pretty much bored with the way things are. While exploring, she discovers that a door in the drawing room, behind which has always been a wall of bricks, now has a tunnel to what she assumes is the flat on the other side. But when she goes through, she finds a weird alternate universe where her parents have buttons for eyes, things are interesting, and the world ends beyond the garden...<br /><br />Gaiman mentions in an interview after the book (found only in the ebook edition) that Coraline is usually seen by children as an adventure story, by adults as a horror novel. Both are correct, of course. It is a lovely rendition of both, told in an almost classical children's-book style (consider the diction in older children's books, from the depression or before, and then consider Coraline) but without ever talking down to its target audience. Coraline is a wonderfully well-drawn character, as are most of the book's creations. There is a great deal to enjoy here; this is easily Gaiman's best aside from American Gods. If you've been avoiding it because you thought it was a kids' book, think again. **** </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2857987455198246243">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1018505138" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19590155-vane-j" class="left imgcol" title="Vane J."><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1443339219p2/19590155.jpg" alt="Vane J." /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1018505138?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 24, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19590155-vane-j" class="user" title="Vane J.">Vane J.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=horror" class="actionLinkLite">horror</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=children" class="actionLinkLite">children</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=2015" class="actionLinkLite">2015</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=holy-shite-me-scared" class="actionLinkLite">holy-shite-me-scared</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/19590155-vane-j?shelf=dark-as-my-soul" class="actionLinkLite">dark-as-my-soul</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1018505138">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9304218938370796881"><a rel="nofollow" href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/"> <img width="350" height="117" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png" /></a><br /><br /><strong>Review also posted <a rel="nofollow" href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/2015/10/22/review-coraline-one-of-the-most-unsettling-books-ive-read/">here</a></strong><br /><br /><strong>4.5 out of 5 stars</strong><br /><br />I had watched the movie Coraline 4 years ago but I never knew it was originally a book until earlier this year. Yeah, I know, it’s shameful, but what can we do? Anyway, since I liked the movie, I told myself I was gonna love the book too, thus I added it to my TBR.<br /><br />I had forgotten about it until my recent post about quiet and jumpy horror. I wasn’t sure what books to use for the quiet category, so I asked Evelyn and she mentioned this. Obviously, my intri</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9304218938370796881"><a rel="nofollow" href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/">
  <img width="350" height="117" class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433653616i/15127136._SX540_.png" /></a><br /><br /><strong>Review also posted <a rel="nofollow" href="https://bookswithchemistry.wordpress.com/2015/10/22/review-coraline-one-of-the-most-unsettling-books-ive-read/">here</a></strong><br /><br /><strong>4.5 out of 5 stars</strong><br /><br />I had watched the movie Coraline 4 years ago but I never knew it was originally a book until earlier this year. Yeah, I know, it’s shameful, but what can we do? Anyway, since I liked the movie, I told myself I was gonna love the book too, thus I added it to my TBR.<br /><br />I had forgotten about it until my recent post about quiet and jumpy horror. I wasn’t sure what books to use for the quiet category, so I asked Evelyn and she mentioned this. Obviously, my intrigue was gonna wake up again. And it did, in fact. One week later, I started this book.<br /><br />For those of you who don’t know the story, I’ll tell you a brief synopsis: There’s a girl who feels her parents ignore her and she desires they pay more attention to her, she finds a secret door that leads to a place that’s identical to her home, with replicas of all the people who live there, but this place seems…better. It’s more fun and she can do all she wants. The difference is everyone here has buttons for eyes, and Coraline’s mother wants her for herself, so things start to get bad.<br /><br />The first thing you will notice about this book is its eerie atmosphere. Evelyn was right when she classified it as quiet horror. It’s creepy, but it’s more of those that slowly escalate on you until you’re terrified.<br /><br />Coraline herself is a great character. She’s brave, adventurous and astute. She actually felt her age (around 12 yo) – not too naive and not too mature. She was intelligent, and she was not easily fooled.<br /><br /><blockquote>“Because,” she said, “when you’re scared but you still do it anyway, that’s brave.”</blockquote><br /><br />The cat was another great character. He was so snarky. I was so surprised about the fact that I found myself liking him, because as you well know, I despise cats, but I couldn’t hate him.<br /><br />When reading horror books, there’s a phrase that’s used all the time. This line is: “This book gave me nightmares.” More often than not, this is an exageration, but when I say this book scared me more than any Stephen King book ever had, I am not lying to you – it really did. Who likes people with button eyes that eat bettles and disfigurate, huh?<br /><br />It’s interesting to notice too what Neil Gaiman said in a note at the end of the book:<br /><br /><blockquote>I learned when people began to read it, that children experienced as an adventure, but which gave adults nightmares.</blockquote><br /><br />I’ve been wondering why that happens. Can it be that children see it as a quest for Coraline to save herself and her parents from the clutches of her evil other mother but adults or mature readers as a story in which the figures who are supposed to make us feel safe are so corrupted they scare? Or is it something else entirely?<br /><br />The illustrations were another point in the book’s favour. They captured perfectly the creepiness and they accompanied the best scenes. For example, look at this work:<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1445550930i/16669455.jpg" /><br /><br />Some goosebumps it gives you, right?<br /><br />Anyway, I’m glad I finally read this book, and I can’t wait to read more macabre things by Neil Gaiman. Now I’ll go <s>sew my eyes shut</s> take better care of myself and be wary of rats <s>and spiders</s>.<br /><br />___________________________________________<br /><br /><strong>Pre-review (October 21, 2015)</strong><br /><br />Such a great book. I'm wondering whether I should rate it 4 or 5 stars. It was creepy and there's no way I'll get over some of the illustrations. I want more Neil Gaiman NOW.<br /><br />RTC.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15363879040479243372">this book makes me really cross i missed the 3d movie when it was out. there are definitely things i would have loved to have seen all up in my face. i think if i had read this as a young girl, it would be one of my favorite books ever. as a (physical) adult, i enjoyed it, but ive read too much in my life to be scared of it, or surprised by it, which is a shame. im going to turn this review into a request for people to scare me. when i was little, my brother would hide under my bed until after i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15363879040479243372">this book makes me really cross i missed the 3d movie when it was out. there are definitely things i would have loved to have seen all up in my face. i think if i had read this as a young girl, it would be one of my favorite books ever. as a (physical) adult, i enjoyed it, but ive read too much in my life to be scared of it, or surprised by it, which is a shame. im going to turn this review into a request for people to scare me. when i was little, my brother would hide under my bed until after i was just drifting off to sleep, and then jump out to scare me. it worked. when i was a little older, and he was babysitting me, he would rent the scariest movies and make me watch them with him. he never really liked me. so but now it is rare for me to get scared. and i want to be scared. the last book to scare me was when i was about 8 or 9 and i was going on a car drive with family, and someone had left a stephen king book on the floor of the car, and i ran out of my own books so i picked it up and read that boogeyman story. didnt sleep for months. thats what i want. a book, a movie, i dont care. someone scare me. (just dont hide under my bed - lets stick to books or movies, yeah?)this will be my preparation for halloween mental gathering.</span>

  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1134487331" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5253785-lyn" class="left imgcol" title="Lyn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1428721461p2/5253785.jpg" alt="Lyn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1134487331?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 08, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5253785-lyn" class="user" title="Lyn">Lyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1134487331">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4508971080576330730">Coraline, not Caroline, thank you, the little girl who was small for her age, and found herself in darkest danger was the subject of Neil Gaiman’s 2002 publication, which was in Gaiman’s own words “refreshingly creepy.”<br /><br />Gaiman said that he started writing the book for his young daughter Holly around the time they moved to America but, unintentionally, wrote it very slowly, “one word at a time” and thus stretched out the project for years. Refreshingly creepy is maybe the best way to describe this</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4508971080576330730">Coraline, not Caroline, thank you, the little girl who was small for her age, and found herself in darkest danger was the subject of Neil Gaiman’s 2002 publication, which was in Gaiman’s own words “refreshingly creepy.”<br /><br />Gaiman said that he started writing the book for his young daughter Holly around the time they moved to America but, unintentionally, wrote it very slowly, “one word at a time” and thus stretched out the project for years. Refreshingly creepy is maybe the best way to describe this young adult work that also has darker elements, references to myth and the occult that will probably fly over the heads of younger readers. Older readers will find Coraline living down the street from Charles Addams place and also backyard neighbors of Ray Bradbury’s <a title="The October Country by Ray Bradbury" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/93251.The_October_Country">The October Country</a> folks.<br /><br />“There was a tiny doubt inside her, like a maggot in an apple core.”<br /><br />But Gaiman’s Coraline never achieves the campy fun of Addams or Bradbury, leaning instead towards a Tim Burtonesque darkness that is charming in its own way. (Though the 2009 film was directed by Burton collaborator Henry Selick).<br /><br />Gaiman masterfully blends haunting elements of nighttime mystery with his own inimitable style of writing, to create a setting for Coraline to explore. Coraline’s plucky little girl, written soberly for a slightly more mature reader, struggles perfectly with the arcane machinations of the other mother.<br /><br />“It doth not hurt,” whispered one faint voice.<br /><br />Finally, Gaiman’s unique ability to craft a sepulchral niche that is akin to Lovecraft but more playful, reminds the reader of his brilliant work <a title="The Graveyard Book by Neil Gaiman" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2213661.The_Graveyard_Book">The Graveyard Book</a>. An excellent introduction to his canon, this is also a must read for a Gaiman fan.<br /><br /><img width="236" height="364" class="escapedImg" alt="description" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1441714163i/16142990.jpg" /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4508971080576330730">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_206420630">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/206420630" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1886642-catie" class="left imgcol" title="Catie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" alt="Catie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/206420630?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 11, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1886642-catie" class="user" title="Catie">Catie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/1154164.Coraline" title="Audio CD 9780060510480" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2011" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=children-s" class="actionLinkLite">children-s</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=graphic-illustrated-novels" class="actionLinkLite">graphic-illustrated-novels</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=me-and-the-girls" class="actionLinkLite">me-and-the-girls</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio" class="actionLinkLite">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer206420630">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2788577970880050608">This would be a perfect choice for a road trip with small children (maybe age seven and up or so). It’s an incredibly imaginative, quirky adventure that’s simple yet not excruciatingly so. I felt entertained throughout, and some of the dialogue had me laughing out loud. There’s no question that this book is creeeeeepy but I’m one of those people that believes kids can handle a lot more than watered down fluff books. Coraline is such a wonderful heroine: she’s a clever, matter of fact, singular g</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2788577970880050608">This would be a perfect choice for a road trip with small children (maybe age seven and up or so). It’s an incredibly imaginative, quirky adventure that’s simple yet not excruciatingly so. I felt entertained throughout, and some of the dialogue had me laughing out loud. There’s no question that this book is creeeeeepy but I’m one of those people that believes kids can handle a lot more than watered down fluff books. Coraline is such a wonderful heroine: she’s a clever, matter of fact, singular girl with an awesome fashion sense (Day-glo green gloves and yellow wellington boots that look like frogs? YES.) and a quiet determination to succeed even though no one takes her seriously. The stakes are high, the villain is completely unsettling and evil, and Coraline is alone, but she triumphs! It is very satisfying.<br /><br />Coraline (who everyone mistakenly calls Caroline) lives in a big old house, once a large estate, but now divided up into flats. Her parents are constantly unavailable and absorbed with boring work on their computers, except for when her Dad wants to try out a crazy recipe or her Mum wants to go shopping for boring school clothes. There’s no one for her to play with except the eccentric Misses Spink and Forcible, former actresses, and the old man in the attic who claims to be the ring leader for a mouse circus. More than anything, Coraline wants something new, an adventure, even if it might be dangerous. <br /><br />“<em>On the first day Coraline's family moved in, Miss Spink and Miss Forcible made a point of telling Coraline how dangerous the well was, and they warned her to be sure she kept away from it. So Coraline set off to explore for it, so that she knew where it was, to keep away from it properly.”</em><br /><br />This book is exceedingly quotable; the paperback is only one hundred sixty two pages, but there are three pages of quotes currently listed on goodreads. I particularly loved Coraline’s conversations with the cat:<br /><br />“<em>What's your name,' Coraline asked the cat. 'Look, I'm Coraline. Okay?'<br />'Cats don't have names,' it said.<br />'No?' said Coraline.<br />'No,' said the cat. 'Now you people have names. That's because you don't know who you are. We know who we are, so we don't need names.”</em><br /><br />Definitely another cat for the “best talking cats” list. The writing is spare but still manages to be atmospheric and inventive. This quote is so simple, but it’s one of my favorites:<br /><br />“<em>The sky had never seemed so sky; the world had never seemed so world."</em><br /><br />Finally, I have to mention that this audiobook is narrated by the author and he does an AMAZING job. If I could have one person narrate my life, it would be Neil Gaiman.<br /><br /><u>Perfect Musical Pairing</u><br /><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JOm3nrSWRpA">The Rat’s Song</a><br /><br />This is the audiobook version of the Rat’s Song that Neil Gaiman wrote for the book. It appears in segments in the book, and in the audio version (as you’ll see) it is chanted in eerie, echoing verses. I listened to this while walking through heavy fog right before sunrise and it was CREEPY. Enjoy! Try not to have too many nightmares.<br /><br />Also seen on <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/02/ya-review-coraline-by-neil-gaiman.html">The Readventurer</a>.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_45446711">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/45446711" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1670108-jason" class="left imgcol" title="Jason"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1350445084p2/1670108.jpg" alt="Jason" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/45446711?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 06, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1670108-jason" class="user" title="Jason">Jason</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17061.Coraline" title="Paperback 9780061139376" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer45446711">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9055493672682900087">There's something about the way Neil Gaiman writes that appeals to me greatly. He doesn't WASTE words. No flowery, adjective laden descriptions or ridiculous cliches. And yet, I never feel cheated. He'll often move a character from one place or situation to the next, and if you're new to him or have been reading someone else you might think for a second "That was abrupt", but he does it well and it serves the story.<br /><br />More importantly, Coraline is an engrossing tale. Firstly, while Coraline the cha</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9055493672682900087">There's something about the way Neil Gaiman writes that appeals to me greatly. He doesn't WASTE words. No flowery, adjective laden descriptions or ridiculous cliches. And yet, I never feel cheated. He'll often move a character from one place or situation to the next, and if you're new to him or have been reading someone else you might think for a second "That was abrupt", but he does it well and it serves the story.<br /><br />More importantly, Coraline is an engrossing tale. Firstly, while Coraline the character isn't particularly warm or cute, she's smart, inquisitive, polite... you feel bad for her in the boring life she's so unsatisfied with, and in the journey she takes from there. And she's brave, while still admitting her fears and insecurities. And all of this is done without wasting words and while maintaining a reading level that kids could follow.<br /><br />The best part about Coraline is the fun, interesting, vivid story. Neil Gaiman creates an imaginary world here that still feels like it could exist. He doesn't explain away the differences between the book's world and ours with magic or science; his fantasy world exists in or world, and it doesn't feel like it couldn't or shouldn't. And what a world it is. "Other" parents in a house just like yours but better (and far worse) in the subtlest of ways. Keys, mists, a talking cat and ghosts... all done with a class and timelessness that others in the genre (that I'm familiar with anyway) have failed to pull off (but not to attempt).<br /><br />It also seems like Coraline is just begging to be read aloud. Plenty of other books are this way too, but it's obvious that Gaiman knows how to write a story that kids and parents will enjoy cuddling up together with.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9055493672682900087">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1029898271">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1029898271" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4728718-algernon" class="left imgcol" title="Algernon"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451037240p2/4728718.jpg" alt="Algernon" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1029898271?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 28, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4728718-algernon" class="user" title="Algernon">Algernon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/2808945-coraline" title="Paperback 9780061649691" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/4728718-algernon?shelf=2014" class="actionLinkLite">2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1029898271">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2160250595225358161">[9/10]<br /><br /><strong> "I don't think you can be too old for Coraline." </strong><br /><br />To my great delight I discovered this little gem of a story just as I'm about to turn 50, and my enjoyment is I believe proof enough that I haven't turned yet into a cranky and bitter ogre. Neil Gaiman himself, in the afterword, declares his personal affection for the spunky young heroine of the tale:<br /><br /><em> More than ten years ago I started to write a children's book. It was for my daughter, Holly, who was five years old. I wanted it to have a gi</em></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2160250595225358161">[9/10]<br /><br /><strong> "I don't think you can be too old for Coraline." </strong><br /><br />To my great delight I discovered this little gem of a story just as I'm about to turn 50, and my enjoyment is I believe proof enough that I haven't turned yet into a cranky and bitter ogre. Neil Gaiman himself, in the afterword, declares his personal affection for the spunky young heroine of the tale:<br /><br /><em> More than ten years ago I started to write a children's book. It was for my daughter, Holly, who was five years old. I wanted it to have a girl as a heroine, and I wanted it to be refreshingly creepy. </em><br /><br />Mission accomplished. Like in the best tales of the brothers Grimm, Coraline is not about fluffy teddybears or cute orphaned ducklings, but about dark, scary monsters that try to eat you whole in a bite or two, it is about the persistence of evil and the need to stand up and fight against it. It is not a coincidence that the quote selected by Gaiman as an opening gambit is from G K Chesterton. Good fairy tales have important lessons to impart to the readers:<br /><br /><em> "Fairy tales are more than true: not because they tell us that dragons exist, but because they tell us that dragons can be beaten." </em><br /><br />Coraline has a 'dragon' to slay, and she has only herself to blame for the troubles she finds herself in. You see, she was restless, bored by a rainy day, in need of entertainment, looking for some adventure. And her parents were too busy to help her.<br /><br /><em> "What should I do?" asked Coraline.<br />"Read a book", said her mother. "Watch a video. Play with your toys. Go and pester Miss Spink and Miss Forcible, or the crazy old man upstairs."<br />"No", said Coraline. "I don't want to do those things. I want to explore."<br />"I don't really mind what you do", said Coraline's mother, "as long as you don't make a mess." </em><br /><br />Her parents love her truly, but such a hyperactive kid can be trying when you have a deadline or three pots cooking on the stove. So she's left more or less to her own devices, and what she loves best is to go exploring. And the most enticing things are of course those that are forbidden, or locked - the mysteries, the secret places, the white spots on the maps of far distant lands. In her old house this means a locked door that leads to an unoccupied apartment in the same building.<br /><br />Neil Gaiman has used the plot device before, these portals that can be found in the most ordinary places: inside a cupboard, under the stairs, down a rabbit hole, inside a metro station, behind a gate in an ancient stone wall. They take you into a alternate reality existing side by side with the ordinary world (Neverwhere, Stardust, The Ocean At The End of the Lane) where old gods, unicorns, flying sailships, talking frogs and/or wizards roam freely. Coraline accidentaly on purpose steps through into such a world, apparently a copy of her real house and family where her every wish can be granted. But pretty soon, she discovers that the price she has to pay to have her fun is much to high, and she will need all her courage, and boldness and inventiveness if she wants to survive and to help the people she loves most dearly. With a little help from her friends (among them a wonderful sarcastic), she might prevail, but not before the reader is thoroughly scared.<br /><br />In a way, I am glad the author took his time with the story (more than ten years) because it really feels flawless, not a word out of place of unnecessary, all the secondary characters interesting and intriguing. The experience is enhanced by one of Neil Gaiman's long term collaborators, the artist Dave McKean who did most of the covers for Sandman: <em> ... and the pictures are very creepy, and very odd and very true. He even went to the house I used to lived in Nutley, Sussex, and drew it. </em> confides the author in the same interview at the end. I'm not a great fan of stop motion animation, but I am willing to give it one more chance in order to watch the movie version of the novella.<br /><br />In conclusion: Coraline is one of the greatest heroines in fantasy, even if she is "a little small for her age" , and she reminds me not only of Lewis Carrol's Alice, but also of my recent darling - the girl named September from Catherynne Valente's Fairyland books. Kindred spirits, they are all resourceful, intelligent, courageous and playful. I am grateful for being able to take part in their adventures.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2160250595225358161">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
